وقال النووي: هو قول جمهور العلماء، وقال الليث : أجمع المسلمون على أن كثير الرضاع وقليله يحرم في المهد كما يفطر الصائم، والخلاف الثاني: أن مدة الرضاع ثلاثون شهراً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما سنتان، وعند زفر ثلاث سنين، ولنا: أن إرضاع الكبير منسوخ بقوله علية: "لا رضاع بعد فصال ولا يتم بعد احتلام"، رواه أبو داود، ولهما: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلادَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۳) وقوله: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلاثُونَ شَهْرا (الأحقاف:١٥) وأقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، فبقي الفصال حولان وبه قالت الثلاثة، إلا أن مالكاً زاد أياماً . على السنتين ولم يحدها، وله قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالاً عَنْ تَرَاضٍ مِنْهُمَا وَتَشَاوُرِ﴾ (البقرة:۲۳۳) بعد قوله: وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ فثبت أن بعد الحولين رضاع. والمعنى فيه : أنه لا يمكن قطع الولد عن اللبن دفعة واحدة فلابد من زيادة مدة يعتاد فيها الصبي مع اللبن للفطام، فيكون غذاؤه اللبن تارة، والطعام أخرى إلى أن ينسى اللبن، وأقل مدة تنتقل بها العادة ستة أشهر اعتباراً بمدة الحبل، وزفر قدر الزيادة بالحول الكامل؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربعة، ولأبي حنيفة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ﴾ (الأحقاف: ١٥)؛ لأن الله تعالى ذكر شيئين وضرب لهما ،مدة، فكانت مدة الكل منهما على الكمال، فكأنه قال: "حمله ثلاثون شهراً وفصاله ثلاثون شهراً"، فإن قيل: فلماذا حكمتم بأن أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان، قلنا: لقول عائشة هما: الولد لا يبقى في بطن أمه أكثر من سنتين ولو بفلكة مغزل، وجاز هذا بخبر الواحد؛ لأن الآية مأولة وهي في إثبات الحكم مثل القياس. (مستخلص، عيني)
من
في ثلاثين شهرا: أي إذا وجد الرضاع فيها وهي سنتان ونصف عنده وقالا سنتان وبه يفتى. (ط،ع) ما حرم في محل الرفع فاعل لقوله : "حرم" . (ع) بالنسب: أي حرم بسبب الرضاع الذي حرم بسبب النسب. (ع) إلا أم أخيه استثناء من قوله: "حرم" "به" أي يجوز أن يتزوج بهما من الرضاع، ولا يجوز أن بهما يتزوج النسب. (ع)] وكذا أم أخته من الرضاع، ولا يجوز أن يتزوج أم أخيه من النسب؛ لأنه في النسب إن كانت أختاً لأب وأم أو لأم فأم الأخت أمه، وإن كانت أختاً لأب فأم الأخت موطوءة أبيه، وكذا أختاً لابنه وبنته من الرضاعة، ولا يجوز ذلك من النسب؛ لأن أخت ابنه أو بنته من النسب إن كانت منه بأن كانا من أب وأم أو أب فهي بنته، وإن لم تكن منه بأن كانا من أم فهي ربيبته، فإن بنتها تحرم بالدخول، والرضاع في المسألة الأولى يجوز أن يكون متعلقاً بالأم، وأن يكون متعلقا بأخيه، وأن يكون كليهما. وكذا في الثانية يجوز أن يكون متعلقاً بالأخت أو بالابن أو بكليهما، وكل ما لا يحرم من النسب لا يحرم من الرضاع، وقد يحرم من الرضاع كما في الصورتين المذكورتين وههنا صور أخرى تجوز من الرضاع دون النسب، الأولى: يجوز له أن يتزوج بأم حفده من الرضاع دون النسب الثانية: يجوز له أن يتزوج بجدة ولده من الرضاع =
من
Within thirty months, what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by fosterage, except the mother of his brother and the sister of his son... The first: he may marry the mother of his grandchildren from fosterage but not from lineage. The second: he may marry the grandmother of his child from fosterage...
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage primarily explains a ruling of fosterage: generally, fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage, but there are exceptions. The matn states that within the thirty-month period of fosterage, what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by fosterage, except the mother of one's brother from fosterage and the sister of one's son from fosterage. The commentary clarifies that these two individuals are permitted in marriage despite fosterage, while they would be prohibited by lineage due to consanguinity. The passage also includes a summary of the intra-Hanafi dispute on the duration of fosterage (Abu Hanifa: 30 months; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: 2 years; Zufar: 3 years), but this is secondary to the main ruling on exceptions. The commentator explains the reasoning: in lineage, the mother of one's brother is one's own mother (if full or maternal brother) or a wife of one's father (if paternal brother), and the sister of one's son is one's daughter or stepdaughter. Fosterage does not create such close ties, so those marriages are allowed. Additional exceptions include the mother of one's foster grandchildren and the grandmother of one's foster child.

Key Terms
أم الأخ من الرضاع (umm al-akh min al-rada'): The mother of one's brother through fosterage (i.e., the woman who nursed one's foster-brother).
أخت الابن من الرضاع (ukht al-ibn min al-rada'): The sister of one's son through fosterage (i.e., the daughter of the woman who nursed one's foster-son).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Marrying the daughter of one's foster-son

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows marriage to the mother of one's foster-brother and the sister of one's foster-son, despite the general rule that fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits.

The Maximum Period for Radi' – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-madhhab dispute on the maximum suckling period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar on the maximum period of radi', explain their evidence, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
30 months? 2 years? 3 years? The maximum suckling period that prohibits marriage is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses a crucial intra-Hanafi debate: how long after birth does suckling (radi') create marital prohibitions? The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq gives a ruling based on 30 months, but the commentators present a three-way split among Abu Hanifa, his two main students (the Sahibayn), and Zufar. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school uses Quranic verses and hadith, and which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
What exactly is being contested? The maximum time after birth during which a child's suckling can create a foster relationship that prohibits marriage.
The dispute is over duration, not the principle that radi' creates prohibition.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: 30 months; Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): 2 years; Zufar: 3 years.
The matn implies 30 months, but the commentary explains the differences.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on Quran 46:15 (combined pregnancy and weaning = 30 months) and a hadith from Aisha on maximum pregnancy. Sahibayn rely on Quran 2:233 (two years suckling) and the need for gradual weaning. Zufar uses a full year for habit transfer.
Each side uses both textual and rational arguments.
4
Understand the tarjih
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of the Sahibayn: 2 years. The commentary states 'Wa qala sana wa bihi yafta' (they said two years and thus is issued fatwa).
Later Hanafi authorities preferred this view.
5
Apply the thamarah
Practical consequence: If a child is suckled after 2 years, no prohibition according to mufta bihi; if within 30 months, prohibition according to Abu Hanifa; if within 3 years, prohibition according to Zufar.
Fatwa follows 2 years, but one may act on the other views for precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرضاع أحكام الرضاع في ثلاثين شهرا ما حرم بالنسب إلا أم أخيه وأخت ابنه. وقال النووي: هو قول جمهور العلماء، وقال الليث: أجمع المسلمون على أن كثير الرضاع وقليله يحرم في المهد كما يفطر الصائم، والخلاف الثاني: أن مدة الرضاع ثلاثون شهراً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما سنتان، وعند زفر ثلاث سنين، ولنا: أن إرضاع الكبير منسوخ بقوله عليه: "لا رضاع بعد فصال ولا يتم بعد احتلام"، رواه أبو داود، ولهما: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلادَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۳) وقوله: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلاثُونَ شَهْراً﴾ (الأحقاف:١٥) وأقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، فبقي الفصال حولان وبه قالت الثلاثة، إلا أن مالكاً زاد أياماً على السنتين ولم يحدها، وله قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالاً عَنْ تَرَاضٍ مِنْهُمَا وَتَشَاوُرِ﴾ (البقرة:۲۳۳) بعد قوله: وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ فثبت أن بعد الحولين رضاع. والمعنى فيه: أنه لا يمكن قطع الولد عن اللبن دفعة واحدة فلابد من زيادة مدة يعتاد فيها الصبي مع اللبن للفطام، فيكون غذاؤه اللبن تارة، والطعام أخرى إلى أن ينسى اللبن، وأقل مدة تنتقل بها العادة ستة أشهر اعتباراً بمدة الحبل، وزفر قدر الزيادة بالحول الكامل؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربعة، ولأبي حنيفة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ﴾ (الأحقاف: ١٥)؛ لأن الله تعالى ذكر شيئين وضرب لهما مدة، فكانت مدة الكل منهما على الكمال، فكأنه قال: حمله ثلاثون شهراً وفصاله ثلاثون شهراً، فإن قيل: فلماذا حكمتم بأن أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان، قلنا: لقول عائشة رضي الله عنها: الولد لا يبقى في بطن أمه أكثر من سنتين ولو بفلكة مغزل، وجاز هذا بخبر الواحد؛ لأن الآية مأولة وهي في إثبات الحكم مثل القياس.
The Book of Radi'. Rulings of Radi'. Within thirty months, what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited [by radi'], except the mother of one's brother and the sister of one's son. Al-Nawawi said: This is the statement of the majority of scholars. Al-Layth said: The Muslims are agreed that much and little of radi' prohibits while in the cradle, just as it breaks the fast of the fasting person. The second difference is that the period of radi' is thirty months according to Abu Hanifa, two years according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and three years according to Zufar. Our proof: The suckling of an older child was abrogated by his saying: 'No radi' after weaning, and no orphanage after puberty,' narrated by Abu Dawud. Their proof: Allah's saying: 'Mothers shall suckle their children two complete years' (al-Baqara 233) and His saying: 'His bearing and his weaning are thirty months' (al-Ahqaf 15). The minimum period of pregnancy is six months, so the weaning period remains two years, and the three (Abu Hanifa's students) said this, except that Malik added some days to the two years without specifying a limit. Their proof (also): Allah's saying: 'If they both desire weaning by mutual consent and consultation' (al-Baqara 233) after His saying: 'Mothers shall suckle their children,' so it is established that there is radi' after two years. The meaning of it is that it is not possible to cut off the child from milk all at once, so an additional period is necessary during which the child becomes accustomed to milk for weaning; thus his food is sometimes milk and sometimes food until he forgets the milk. The minimum period by which the habit is transferred is six months, by analogy with the duration of pregnancy. Zufar estimated the increase at a full year because it includes the four seasons. Abu Hanifa's proof: Allah's saying: 'His bearing and his weaning are thirty months' (al-Ahqaf 15); because Allah mentioned two things and set one duration for them, so the duration of each of them is complete, as if He said: 'His bearing is thirty months and his weaning is thirty months.' If it is said: Why did you rule that the maximum period of pregnancy is two years? We say: Because of the saying of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): A child does not remain in its mother's womb more than two years, even if it were a spindle's whorl. And this is permissible through a solitary report because the verse is interpreted (ta'wil) and it is like qiyas in establishing the ruling.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum duration for radi' (suckling) that causes marriage prohibition. The base text (matn) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: 'Within thirty months, what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited [by radi'], except the mother of one's brother and the sister of one's son.' The commentator then presents the dispute clearly: Abu Hanifa holds that the limit is 30 months (two and a half years), his two foremost students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is two years, and Zufar holds it is three years. The commentary then provides proofs for both sides. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) relies on the verse in al-Ahqaf where Allah mentions the combined duration of pregnancy and weaning as 30 months, interpreted as each being 30 months. The Sahibayn rely on the verse in al-Baqarah prescribing two years of suckling and the verse permitting weaning by consent after two years, implying suckling can occur after two years. The dispute also involves logical arguments about the minimum time for habit transfer and maximum pregnancy duration. The passage concludes with Abu Hanifa's response supporting his view with a hadith from Aisha about maximum pregnancy. This is a classic example of istinbat (legal derivation) from the Quran using both apparent meaning (zahir) and analogy (qiyas).

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): The nursing or suckling of a child by a woman other than his mother, which creates a foster relationship that prohibits marriage.
فصال (fisal): Weaning, the act of accustoming a child to stop nursing and rely on other food.
حولين (hawlayn): Two complete years, the minimum recommended period of suckling according to the Quran (2:233).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what is the maximum period during which radi' causes marriage prohibition?
A) 30 months
B) 2 years
C) 3 years
D) Until the child is weaned regardless of age

Key Takeaway
The maximum period for radi' causing marriage prohibition is 2 years according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn), not 30 months (Abu Hanifa) or 3 years (Zufar).

Exceptions to Radi' Prohibition: Two Key Cases and the General Principle
Explanation of rada' exceptions with reasoning and additional cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptions where radi' permits marriage that lineage prohibits and explain the underlying principle that rada' does not mirror lineage exactly.

Core Idea
Rada' prohibits what lineage prohibits, but not identically; some relationships are permissible only by rada'.

In the previous lesson, we learned that rada' (foster-kinship) creates prohibitions similar to lineage. However, there are exceptions where rada' permits a marriage that would be prohibited by lineage. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states two such exceptions: the mother of one's foster brother and the sister of one's foster son. In this lesson, we will explore these exceptions, the reasoning behind them, and additional cases that illustrate the general principle that rada' and lineage prohibitions are parallel but not identical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions from the matn
List the two exceptions stated in the text: the mother of one's foster brother (umm akhih min al-rada') and the sister of one's foster son (ukht ibnihi min al-rada').
These are the only exceptions given in the matn.
2
Understand the lineage analogy
For each exception, explain why marriage would be prohibited by lineage. For the mother of one's brother: by lineage, she is one's own mother (if full or maternal half-brother) or stepmother (if paternal half-brother). For the sister of one's son: by lineage, she is one's daughter (if from both parents or father) or stepdaughter (if from mother only, and her daughter is prohibited after consummation).
The commentary provides this reasoning.
3
Apply the rada' principle
Explain why rada' does not create the same prohibition in these cases. In rada', the wet nurse who suckled both the child and her own son is not a 'mother' to the child; she is merely a milk-giver. Similarly, the sister of the foster son shares milk with him but is not a 'daughter' to the foster sibling.
The milk relationship does not transfer all lineage ties.
4
Expand to additional cases
List the seven additional cases mentioned in the commentary where rada' permits marriage that lineage prohibits. These include: mother of one's foster grandson, grandmother of one's foster child, paternal aunt of one's foster son, father of one's foster brother (for women), mother of one's foster paternal uncle, mother of one's foster maternal uncle, and brother of one's foster daughter (for women).
These further illustrate the pattern.
5
Derive the general principle
State the rule: Whatever is not prohibited by lineage is not prohibited by rada'. However, rada' may sometimes prohibit what lineage does not (the reverse is not true; these exceptions show the opposite: lineage prohibits what rada' does not). So the relationship is asymmetrical: rada' prohibitions are a subset of lineage prohibitions, but not all lineage prohibitions apply.
This principle is derived from the commentary's statement 'wa kullu ma la yahrumu min al-nasabi la yahrumu min al-rada'' (whatever is not prohibited by lineage is not prohibited by rada').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ثلاثين شهرا: أي إذا وجد الرضاع فيها وهي سنتان ونصف عنده وقالا سنتان وبه يفتى. (ط،ع) ما حرم في محل الرفع فاعل لقوله : "حرم" . (ع) بالنسب: أي حرم بسبب الرضاع الذي حرم بسبب النسب. (ع) إلا أم أخيه استثناء من قوله: "حرم" "به" أي يجوز أن يتزوج بهما من الرضاع، ولا يجوز أن بهما يتزوج النسب. (ع)] وكذا أم أخته من الرضاع، ولا يجوز أن يتزوج أم أخيه من النسب؛ لأنه في النسب إن كانت أختاً لأب وأم أو لأم فأم الأخت أمه، وإن كانت أختاً لأب فأم الأخت موطوءة أبيه، وكذا أختاً لابنه وبنته من الرضاعة، ولا يجوز ذلك من النسب؛ لأن أخت ابنه أو بنته من النسب إن كانت منه بأن كانا من أب وأم أو أب فهي بنته، وإن لم تكن منه بأن كانا من أم فهي ربيبته، فإن بنتها تحرم بالدخول، والرضاع في المسألة الأولى يجوز أن يكون متعلقاً بالأم، وأن يكون متعلقا بأخيه، وأن يكون كليهما. وكذا في الثانية يجوز أن يكون متعلقاً بالأخت أو بالابن أو بكليهما، وكل ما لا يحرم من النسب لا يحرم من الرضاع، وقد يحرم من الرضاع كما في الصورتين المذكورتين وههنا صور أخرى تجوز من الرضاع دون النسب، الأولى: يجوز له أن يتزوج بأم حفده من الرضاع دون النسب الثانية: يجوز له أن يتزوج بجدة ولده من الرضاع دون النسب، الثالثة: يجوز له أن يتزوج بعمة ابنه من الرضاع دون النسب، الرابعة: يجوز لها أن تتزوج بأبي أخيها من الرضاع دون النسب الخامسة: يجوز له أن يتزوج أم عمه من الرضاع دون النسب، السادسة: يجوز له أن يتزوج أم خاله من الرضاع دون النسب السابعة: يجوز لها أن تتزوج بأخ ابنتها من الرضاع دون النسب.
Within thirty months: i.e., if she finds radi' within it, and it is two and a half years according to him (Abu Hanifa), and the two (Sahibayn) said two years, and thus is issued fatwa. (T, A) 'What is prohibited' is in the nominative as the subject of 'prohibited'. (A) 'By lineage': i.e., prohibited due to radi' which is prohibited due to lineage. (A) 'Except the mother of one's brother' is an exception from his statement 'prohibited' 'by it' meaning it is permissible to marry both of them from radi', and it is not permissible to marry them by lineage. (A) Similarly the mother of one's sister from radi', and it is not permissible to marry the mother of one's brother from lineage; because in lineage if she is a sister from father and mother or from mother, then the mother of the sister is his mother; and if she is a sister from father, then the mother of the sister is his father's wife (mawtu'a). Similarly, the sister of one's son and daughter from radi' are prohibited from lineage, because the sister of one's son or daughter from lineage, if she is from him by both parents or by father, she is his daughter; and if she is not from him, but from mother, she is his stepdaughter; and indeed her daughter becomes prohibited by consummation. In the first issue, radi' may be attached to the mother, or to one's brother, or to both. Similarly in the second, it may be attached to the sister, to the son, or to both. Whatever is not prohibited in lineage is not prohibited in radi', and sometimes radi' prohibits what lineage does not, as in the two mentioned cases. Here are other cases that are permissible from radi' but not from lineage: First: It is permissible for him to marry the mother of his grandson from radi' but not from lineage. Second: It is permissible for him to marry the grandmother of his child from radi' but not from lineage. Third: It is permissible for him to marry the paternal aunt of his son from radi' but not from lineage. Fourth: It is permissible for her to marry the father of her brother from radi' but not from lineage. Fifth: It is permissible for him to marry the mother of his paternal uncle from radi' but not from lineage. Sixth: It is permissible for him to marry the mother of his maternal uncle from radi' but not from lineage. Seventh: It is permissible for her to marry the brother of her daughter from radi' but not from lineage.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage explains the two exceptions given in the matn where radi' permits marriage that lineage would prohibit. The first is the mother of one's foster brother: if a woman suckles a child, her own son becomes that child's foster brother, but the mother herself is not prohibited to the child by radi' (she is the wet nurse, not a relative by lineage). However, by lineage, the mother of one's brother is one's own mother or stepmother, so marriage is prohibited. The second is the sister of one's foster son: the foster son's sister (through the same wet nurse) is not a relative by radi' to the foster sibling, but by lineage, the sister of one's son is one's daughter or stepdaughter, so marriage is prohibited. The commentary then lists seven additional cases where radi' permits marriage that lineage does not. These cases help clarify the general principle that rada' creates a set of prohibitions analogous to lineage but not identical; exceptions occur due to the specific relationships created by milk-kinship.

Key Terms
أم أخيه (umm akhih): The mother of one's foster brother; in rada', she is the wet nurse who suckled both, but is not prohibited to the foster child.
أخت ابنه (ukht ibnihi): The sister of one's foster son; in rada', she is not a direct relative, so marriage is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an exception where rada' permits marriage that lineage prohibits?
A) The foster mother (the wet nurse) herself
B) The mother of one's foster brother
C) The foster sister
D) The daughter of one's foster son

Key Takeaway
Only certain relationships are prohibited by rada'; the mother of one's foster brother and sister of one's foster son are exceptions permissible to marry, demonstrating that rada' and lineage prohibitions are not identical.

The Hanafi Position on Laban al-Fahl (Milk of the Male)
Inter-madhhab dispute on the prohibition effect of the husband's milk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on laban al-fahl and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The milk attributed to the father creates full marriage prohibitions in Hanafi fiqh, just like lineage.

This passage addresses a disputed issue in Islamic family law: does the milk produced by a woman due to her husband's insemination create a relationship of rada' (fosterage) between the nursling and the husband's relatives? The Hanafi school affirms this, relying on hadith and the principle that rada' mirrors lineage. The Shafi'i school, in one opinion, disagrees, arguing that milk is part of the woman only. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly determining marriage prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the husband (fahl) becomes a father by rada', and his relatives (children, siblings, parents) become mahrams to the nursling.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i (in one qawl) holds that laban al-fahl does not create prohibition. Milk is only a part of the woman.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: prohibition is based on partiality (juz'iyya), and milk is from the woman, not the man.
This argument relies on a specific understanding of the nature of milk.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi proofs: the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet called Aflah her uncle, and the principle that 'what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by radi'. The man is the cause of the milk through pregnancy, so the milk is attributed to him by causality.
The Hanafi proof is dalil naqli (textual evidence).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis prohibit marriage between the nursling and any relative of the fahl; Shafi'is (in that qawl) do not.
This difference has real-world implications for marriage arrangements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزوج مرضعة لبنها منه أب للرضيع، وابنه أخ وبنته أخت وأخوه عم وأخته عمّةٌ أي بنت الزوج أي أخ الزوج للرضيع أي أخت الزوج. وتحل أختُ أخيه رضاعاً ونسباً. لها لبنها منه: [ أي من الزوج والجملة صفة للمرضعة، والمعنى: لبن المرضعة نزل من الزوج، وإن كانت أمة فالسيد والواطئ بشبهة. (ط، ع)] احترز بذلك عن زوج ليس لبنها منه بأن تزوجت ذات لبن، ولبنها بسبب زوج آخر كان من قبل، فأرضعت به صبياً، فإنه لا يكون ولداً له من الرضاع، وإنما يكون ربيبه من الرضاع، حتى يجوز له أن يتزوج بأولاد الزوج الثاني من غيرها، وبأخواته أي أخوات الزوج الثاني كما في النسب، ويكون ولد الزوج الأول ما لم تلد من الثاني، فإذا ولدت منه فأرضعت به صبياً فهو ولد الثاني بالاتفاق؛ لأن اللبن منه، وإن لم تحبل من الثاني، فهو ولد الأول بالاتفاق؛ لأن اللبن منه رمز الحقائق: ۲۲۹/۱] ابنه أخ للرضيع وإن كان من امرأة أخرى. (ط) أخت للرضيع وإن كانت من امرأة أخرى وأبوه جد وأمه جدة. (ط) وأخته عمة: اللرضيع لا تحل مناكحة من هؤلاء كما في النسب فكل هذه القرابات التي بواسطة زوج المرضعة لا تحل مناكحة أحد في النسب وهو معنى قولهم: "لبن" الفحل يتعلق به التحريم، وعند الشافعي في قول: لبن الفحل لا يحرم؛ لأن الحرمة لشبهة البعضية، واللبن بعض المرأة لا بعض الرجل، ولنا ما روي عن عائشة لها أنها قالت: دخل علي أفلح أخو أبي القعيس، فاستترت منه فقال : تستترين مني وأنا عمك ؟ قالت :قلت من أين؟ قال: أرضعتك امرأة أخي، قالت: إنما أرضعتني المرأة و لم يرضعني الرجل، فدخل عليها فحدثته فقال: "إنه عمك فليلج عليك". وفي "الموطأ" سئل ابن عباس الله عن رجل كان له امرأتان فأرضعت إحداهما غلاماً، وأرضعت الأخرى جارية. فقيل له: هل يتزوج الغلام الجارية؟ قال: اللقاح واحد، فثبت أن لبن الفحل يحرم؛ لأن حكمه حكم النسب؛ لقوله عليها: "يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب"، والحرمة في النسب ثبتت من الجانبين أي الرجال والنساء، فكذا الحرمة من الرضاعة والمراد من لبن الفحل لبن حدث من حمل رجل، فلو تزوج امرأة و لم تلد منه، ثم نزل اللبن فهذا اللبن من هذه المرأة، وليس بلبن الفحل وأيضاً الفحل سبب لنزول لبنها بواسطة إحبالها، فينسب اللبن إليه بحكم السببية. (فتح، مستخلص) رضاعاً: أي من حيث الرضاع وهو ظاهر. (ع) ونسباً : أي من حيث النسب بأن يكون له أخ من أب له أخت من أمه حل له أن يتزوجها. (ع)
And the husband of the wet nurse, whose milk is from him, is a father to the nursing infant, and his son is a brother, his daughter is a sister, his brother is an uncle, and his sister is a paternal aunt to the nursing infant, meaning the daughter of the husband, i.e., the brother of the husband is a paternal uncle, and the sister of the husband is a paternal aunt. And the sister of his brother (i.e., the nursing infant's brother) is permissible (to marry) whether by radi' or lineage. His milk is from him: i.e., from the husband, and the phrase is a description of the wet nurse; the meaning is that the milk of the wet nurse comes from the husband, even if she is a slave, then the master or one who has intercourse with her due to a semblance of right (shubha) [is considered]. (T, A) This caution is for a husband whose milk is not from her, if she had milk from another husband previously, and she nursed a child with it, then he is not a son by radi' from him, but rather a stepson by radi', so it is permissible for him to marry the children of the second husband from another woman, and his sisters, i.e., the sisters of the second husband, just as in lineage. And he is a son of the first husband as long as she has not given birth from the second. If she gives birth from the second and then nurses a child, then it is the second's child by agreement, because the milk is from him; and if she did not conceive from the second, it is the first's child by agreement, because the milk is from him. [From Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/229] His son is a brother to the nursing infant even if from another woman. (T) His daughter is a sister to the nursing infant even if from another woman, and his father (the husband's) is a grandfather and his mother is a grandmother. (T) And his sister is a paternal aunt to the infant: it is not permissible to marry these [relatives] just as in lineage; so all these relatives through the husband of the wet nurse are not permissible to marry any of them in lineage, and this is the meaning of their statement: 'The milk of the male (laban al-fahl) entails prohibition.' According to al-Shafi'i in one opinion, laban al-fahl does not cause prohibition, because prohibition is due to resemblance of partiality, and milk is part of the woman, not part of the man. Our proof is what is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: Aflah, the brother of Abu al-Qu'ais, entered upon me, and I screened myself from him. He said: Do you screen yourself from me while I am your uncle? I said: From where? He said: Your brother's wife suckled you. I said: Only the woman suckled me, not the man. So he (the Prophet) entered upon her, and she told him, and he said: 'He is your uncle, so let him enter upon you.' And in the Muwatta', Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about a man who had two wives, one of whom nursed a boy, and the other nursed a girl. It was said to him: Can the boy marry the girl? He said: The milk (semen) is one. So it is established that laban al-fahl prohibits, because its ruling is the ruling of lineage, due to his saying: 'What is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by radi'.' And prohibition in lineage is established from both sides, i.e., men and women. Likewise for radi', and what is meant by laban al-fahl is milk that comes from a man's insemination (pregnancy). If a man married a woman and she did not give birth from him, then milk came down, this milk is from this woman, and it is not laban al-fahl. Additionally, the male is the cause for the descent of her milk by means of causing pregnancy, so the milk is attributed to him by virtue of causality. (From Fath, mustakhlas) 'By radi'': i.e., from the perspective of radi', and it is apparent. (A) 'And by lineage': i.e., from the perspective of lineage, that he has a brother from father and a sister from mother, it is permissible for him to marry her. (A)
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the concept of 'laban al-fahl' (milk of the male). The Hanafi position is that the husband of the wet nurse (whose insemination caused the milk) becomes the 'father' of the nursling through rada', creating a full set of prohibitions: his children become siblings, his parents become grandparents, etc. This is based on the principle that rada' mirrors lineage. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet affirmed that Aflah was her uncle because he was the brother of her wet nurse's husband, and the statement of Ibn Abbas that one man's two wives nursing a boy and a girl makes them siblings. The Shafi'i view (one opinion) denies that laban al-fahl creates prohibition, arguing that milk is a part of the woman, not the man. The Hanafi rebuttal relies on the general hadith 'What is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by radi'' and the principle of causality: the man is the cause of the milk through pregnancy, so the milk is attributed to him. The passage also clarifies that 'laban al-fahl' specifically refers to milk that results from a pregnancy caused by that man; milk that appears without pregnancy is not attributed to him.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): Milk that results from a man's insemination, i.e., milk produced by a woman after giving birth to his child.
فحل (fahl): The male (husband) whose semen causes the pregnancy, making him the 'origin' of the milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the wet nurse's blood relatives
B) Only the wet nurse's husband's blood relatives
C) Both the wet nurse's and her husband's blood relatives
D) Neither, only the wet nurse herself

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that laban al-fahl creates full prohibition by rada', establishing the husband's relatives as mahrams.

Milk of Virgin and Dead Woman: Fosterage Prohibition and Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on dead woman's milk with rational proof and enema exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on milk from a virgin and dead woman for fosterage, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the concept of 'illa.

Core Idea
Milk is milk—its legal effect depends on its reality as a growth-causing substance, not the woman's life.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a clear Hanafi ruling: the milk of a virgin and a dead woman establishes fosterage prohibition. The author then reports the Shafi'i objection and refutes it using rational arguments (dalil 'aqli). Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how Hanafi usul treats 'illa (cause) and the scope of textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main ruling: milk from a virgin and from a dead woman is prohibited for fosterage (i.e., it creates mahramiyyah). Note the exception: enema does not create prohibition.
The ruling covers both virgin and dead woman, but the dispute focuses on the dead woman.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that milk from a dead woman does not create fosterage prohibition. His basis: the woman herself is no longer a locus for rulings; she cannot be a 'mother' after death.
The Shafi'i argument is reasoned from the cessation of legal personhood.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: because the woman is dead, she is not subject to rulings like motherhood; similarly, intercourse with a dead woman does not cause in-law prohibition. Therefore, her milk should not cause fosterage prohibition.
This is an argument by analogy (qiyas) with the case of intercourse.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter: the milk itself is real milk and a cause of growth; the general texts (nusus) about fosterage apply to any milk that produces growth. They also note that rulings do apply to dead women in matters like burial and tayammum.
They distinguish the case of intercourse: prohibition from intercourse is due to the act (meeting of the sexual parts), which ceases with death, but milk is a substance that can exist independently.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a child suckles from a deceased woman, Hanafis consider the fosterage prohibitions to apply (e.g., the child cannot marry the woman's living daughters), while Shafi'is do not.
This difference affects real-world fatwa in cases of post-mortem breastfeeding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبن البكر والميتة محرم لا الاحتقان، وقال الشافعي له: لبن الميتة ليس بمحرم؛ لأن الأصل في ثبوت الحرمة المرأة حتى تصير أما للرضيع، ويتعلق بها الأحكام، وبالموت لم تبق محلاً له، ولهذا لا يوجب وطئها حرمة المصاهرة، ولنا: أنه لبن حقيقة، وهو سبب النشوء والنمو، فيتناوله إطلاق النصوص ولا نسلم أن الحكم لا يثبت في حقها، بل يثبت في حقها دفنا وتيميما، ألا ترى أن لبنها لو حلب في حياتها فأوجر به صبي بعد موتها لما يثبت به التحريم، ولو كان ما ذكره مانعاً لما ثبت، والحرمة بالوطء لكونه ملاقياً محل الحرث، وقد زال بالموت. تبيين الحقائق: ٦٤٠/٢] (فتح) لا الاحتقان: أي لا يحرم الاحتقان بالألبان بلا خلاف بين الأصحاب في رواية الأصول، وبين الأئمة الأربعة وكذا لا يحرم الإقطار في الإحليل والأذن والجائفة والآمة؛ لأن النشوء لا يوجد فيه والتحريم باعتباره، وعن محمد أنه يثبت الحرمة بالاحتقان كما يفسد به الصوم قلنا الفطر يتعلق بالوصول إلى الجوف، والمحرم في الرضاع معنى النشوء، ولا يوجد فيه، وعلى هذا الخلاف الإقطار في الإحليل ،وغيره والسعوط والوجور يثبت بهما التحريم بالاتفاق. (عيني، فتح)
The milk of a virgin and a dead woman is forbidden, not enema. Al-Shafi'i said: The milk of a dead woman is not forbidden because the basis for establishing prohibition is the woman until she becomes a mother to the suckling, and rulings attach to her, and with death she is no longer a locus for it, and therefore intercourse with her does not cause in-law prohibition. Our proof: It is real milk, and it is a cause of growth and development, so the general texts include it, and we do not accept that the ruling is not established regarding her; rather it is established regarding her for burial and tayammum. Do you not see that if her milk were expressed during her life and then administered to an infant after her death, it would not establish prohibition? And if what he mentioned were an impediment, it would not be established. And prohibition by intercourse is due to it meeting the place of tillage, which has ceased with death. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:640] (Fath) 'Not enema': i.e., enema with milk does not cause prohibition without dispute among the companions in the transmitted narration, and among the four imams. Likewise, injection into the urethra, ear, deep wound, and head wound is not prohibited because growth does not occur therein, and prohibition is based on it. From Muhammad: prohibition is established by enema just as it breaks the fast. We said: breaking the fast depends on reaching the stomach, whereas the prohibition in fosterage is the meaning of growth, which does not exist therein. On this basis, injection into the urethra, etc., differs, and snuff and oral administration establish prohibition by agreement. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the milk of a dead woman. The Hanafi position states that milk from a virgin (unmarried woman who has never given birth) and from a dead woman is prohibited for fosterage, meaning it establishes the same kinship prohibitions as breastfeeding from a living woman. The exception is that using such milk as an enema does not create the prohibition. Al-Shafi'i argues that milk from a dead woman cannot create prohibition because the woman herself is no longer a proper subject for rulings; she is dead and cannot become a mother to the suckling. The Hanafis respond by noting that the milk itself is real milk and a cause of growth, so it falls under the general evidence for fosterage. They also point out that rulings do apply to dead women in matters like burial and tayammum. As for enema, it does not cause prohibition because the meaning of growth is absent when milk enters through the anus rather than the mouth. Imam Muhammad is reported to have held that enema does cause prohibition, similar to how it breaks the fast, but the Hanafis distinguish: fasting relates to reaching the stomach, while fosterage relates to growth. Snuff and oral administration, however, do create prohibition by consensus.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage or breastfeeding that establishes kinship prohibitions for marriage.
بكر (bakr): A virgin woman who has never been married or given birth.
ميتة (mayyitah): A deceased woman.
احتقان (ihtiqan): Enema; administration of liquid via the anus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on enema with a woman's milk in terms of fosterage prohibition?
A) It creates prohibition, similar to oral ingestion.
B) It does not create prohibition because growth does not occur.
C) It creates prohibition only if the woman is alive.
D) It is makruh but not haram.

Key Takeaway
For fosterage prohibition, the decisive factor is the milk's inherent quality as a growth-causing substance, not the woman's life status; enema does not trigger prohibition due to absence of growth.

Milk of Man and Goat: No Fosterage Prohibition
Ruling that milk of a man and a goat does not create fosterage prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that male and animal milk do not establish fosterage prohibitions and explain the rational proof based on shubhat al-juz'iyyah.

Core Idea
Only human female milk creates fosterage; male or animal milk does not, because the 'partial share' bond exists only between mother and child.

In this lesson, we examine the scope of fosterage (rada') that creates marriage prohibitions. While it is well known that breastfeeding from a woman establishes prohibition, what about milk from a man or from an animal? The Hanafi school provides a clear and reasoned position based on the concept of partial share (shubhat al-juz'iyyah). This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary explains why only human female milk counts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breastfeeding from a man or a goat. The ruling is that it does NOT create the prohibitions of fosterage.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (aql): fosterage prohibition is established only through the concept of partial share (shubhat al-juz'iyyah) which applies to human mother and child, not to men or animals.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The author argues that milk is real only when it comes from a female capable of childbirth. The partial share is the idea that the child's body is partly formed from the mother's milk. This bond does not exist with male milk or animal milk.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no disagreement within the Hanafi school or across schools on this point; it is muttafaq alayh among Hanafis.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
Practically, if a man produces milk and an infant drinks it, or if a goat's milk is drunk, no fosterage relationship is established, and marriage is not prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبن الرجل: أي لا يحرم أيضاً لبن الرجل؛ لأنه ليس بلبن حقيقة؛ فإن اللبن لا يتصور إلا ممن تتصور منه الولادة، وقوله: "والشاة" أي لا تتعلق الحرمة بلبن الشاة أيضاً؛ لأنها إنما تثبت بطريق الكرامة بواسطة شبهة الجزئية، والأصل فيه المرضعة ثم يتعدى إلى غيرها، ولا جزئية بين الإنسان والبهائم ولاداً فكذا رضاعاً. (فتح)
And the milk of a man: i.e., the milk of a man is also not prohibited because it is not real milk; for milk can only be conceived from someone from whom birth is conceivable. And His saying: 'and the goat' means that prohibition does not attach to the milk of a goat either, because prohibition is established only by way of honor (karamah) through the similarity of partial share (shibh al-juz'iyyah). The origin is the breastfeeding woman, then it extends to others. There is no partial share between humans and animals in birth, thus likewise in fosterage. (Fath)
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: the milk of a man and the milk of a goat do not create the prohibitions of fosterage. The proof is that 'milk' in the context of fosterage refers to human female milk, as it is the only type that can involve the meaning of growth and partial share (juz'iyyah) between mother and child. A man cannot produce milk in this sense; it is not real milk because lactation is only possible for a female who can give birth. As for a goat, even though it produces milk, there is no partial share (resemblance of the body) between humans and animals. The basis of fosterage is the breastfeeding woman, and then the ruling extends to her milk. Since there is no relationship of birth (wiladah) between humans and animals, there is no relationship in fosterage either. Thus, drinking the milk of a man or a goat does not make a woman prohibited for marriage to the man (if he is the one who breastfed) or create any other fosterage prohibitions.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage that establishes marriage prohibitions.
لبن الرجل (laban al-rajul): Milk produced by a man (gynaecomastia or rare condition).
شبهة الجزئية (shubhat al-juz'iyyah): The semblance of a part; the idea that the child shares a part of the mother's body through milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, does breastfeeding from a goat establish fosterage prohibition?
A) Yes, because goat milk causes growth.
B) No, because there is no partial share (juz'iyyah) between humans and animals.
C) Yes, if the goat belongs to a woman.
D) No, but it is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Only human female milk establishes fosterage; male and animal milk have no such effect due to the absence of partial share (shubhat al-juz'iyyah).

Co-wife Breastfeeding the Other: Prohibition and Mahr
Case: Big wife breastfeeds small wife; both become forbidden and mahr implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a co-wife breastfeeds the other and determine the mahr obligations based on intent and consummation.

Core Idea
If a co-wife breastfeeds the other, both become haram; the husband recovers half mahr only if the breastfeeder intentionally corrupted the marriage.

This lesson deals with a unique case in fosterage: when a man's two wives (big and small) are involved such that the big one breastfeeds the small one. The resulting prohibition and the financial consequences (mahr) differ based on the big wife's intent and whether consummation occurred. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the scholarly dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State the basic ruling: if a co-wife breastfeeds the other, both become forbidden to the husband. Cite the Hadith proof.
The prohibition is permanent if consummation occurred.
2
Determine the Mahr for the Big Wife
Analyze the conditions: if separation before consummation, the big wife forfeits her mahr unless she was coerced, asleep, or insane, in which case she receives half.
If after consummation, she gets full mahr but no 'iddah maintenance.
3
Determine the Mahr for the Small Wife
The small wife always receives half mahr because the separation was not from her side.
She is not at fault.
4
Assess the Husband's Recourse
The husband can recover the half mahr paid to the small wife from the big wife only if she intentionally caused the corruption (ta'ammud al-fasad).
Intent requires knowledge of marriage and that breastfeeding spoils it.
5
Evaluate the Scholarly Dispute
Compare Hanafi (require intent) with Shafi'i/Muhammad (always recover) and Maliki (no recovery). Understand the reasoning and the mufta bihi.
The Hanafi position is based on causation requiring transgression.

(ع)] وهذا عندنا، وقال مالك: لا يجب لها شيء؛ لأن الفرقة جاءت من قبلها؛ فإن الارتضاع فعلها، والفرقة باعتباره فسقط مهرها، ولنا: أن الفرقة لا من قبلها وفعلها غير معتبر في إسقاط حقها؛ لأن المهر إنما يسقط جزاء على الفعل، والصغيرة ليست من أهل المجازاة على الفعل، فلا يسقط مهرها حتى لو وجد في الكبيرة أيضاً ما يمنع اعتبار فعلها كالجنون وغيره لا يسقط حقها. (ط) إن تعمدت الفساد: التقييد بتعمد الفساد بالنسبة لرجوع الزوج على الكبيرة بما دفعه للصغيرة، أما سقوط مهر الكبيرة إن كان قبل الوطء فلا يشترط له تعمد الفساد، ثم تعمد الفساد إنما يكون إذا أرضعتها بلا حاجة وعلمت بقيام النكاح، وعلمت أن الإرضاع مفسد، فإن فاتت شيء منه لم تكن متعمدة، فلو ظنت أن الصغيرة جائعةً فأرضعتها ثم تبين أنها شبعانة لا تكون متعمدة، والقول في ذلك قولها؛ لأنه لا يقف عليه غيرها. (مستخلص، فتح) وإلا لا: أي وإن لم تتعمد الفساد أي فساد النكاح بأن فات شيء من الإرضاع بلا حاجة أو العلم بقيام النكاح أو العلم بالإرضاع المفسد لا يرجع بما أدى للصغيرة على الكبيرة، وقال الشافعي ومحمد: يرجع في الوجهين تعمدت الفساد أو لا؛ لأنها أكدت ما كان على شرف السقوط وهو نصف المهر، والتأكيد جار محرى الإتلاف، ولنا: أنها متسببة لا مباشرة؛ لأنها باشرت الإرضاع وهو ليس بموضوع؛ لإفساد النكاح بل هو سبب موضوع للجزئية، وإنما يثبت الفساد في هذه الصورة باتفاق الحال، والمتسبب إنما يضمن بالتعدي وبالرجوع وبه قال زفر وأحمد، وعند مالك: لا يرجع مطلقاً والأصح ما قلنا؛ لأن ضمان التسبب يبني على صفة التعدي وهو تعمد الفساد. رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۱/۱] (فتح) لا: أي لا يرجع به عليها، والقول في ذلك قولها بيمينها إن لم توجد قرينة تدل على تعمدها الفساد. (ط)
And if she breastfeeds her co-wife, they both become forbidden, i.e., if he married a big (one) and a small (one), and the big one breastfed the small one, both become forbidden to the husband because he has combined between a mother and a daughter through fosterage. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:641] That is prohibited. Then if the breastfeeding was before consummation with the big one, it is permissible for him to marry the small one anew, but he may never marry the big one again because she has become the mother of his wife whom he married, so she is permanently forbidden, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Marrying daughters prohibits mothers, and intercourse with mothers prohibits daughters.' If the breastfeeding was after consummation with the big one, both are permanently forbidden. (Mustakhlas) And no mahr is due to the big one because the separation came from her side, so she becomes like one who apostatized before consummation. (Ayni) If he did not have intercourse with her: because the separation came from her before consummation, so it is as if she accepted the husband's son and apostatized. Even if the separation did not come from her – for example if she was coerced, or asleep, and the small one suckled, or a man took the big one's milk and administered it to the small one, or the big one was insane – then she receives half the mahr, because the separation is not attributed to her. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:641] And excluded by his statement 'if he did not have intercourse with her' is: if he did have intercourse with her, then she deserves the entire mahr, but she has no 'iddah maintenance due to her wrongdoing. And he intended by 'intercourse' what is more general than real and legal. (Mustakhlas, Fath) It becomes: and for the small one half of it, and he recovers it from the big one if she intentionally caused corruption, otherwise not. And it is established by that by which property is established. Meaning: the husband intends the big one's intent thereby, even if she did not intentionally cause corruption of the breastfeeding. And for the small one half of it: [i.e., half the mahr because the separation was before consummation not from her side. (Ayni)] This is with us. And Malik said: Nothing is obligatory for her because the separation came from her side, for suckling is her action and separation is based on it, so her mahr is forfeited. Our proof: The separation is not from her side, and her action is not considered in forfeiting her right, because mahr is only forfeited as a penalty for the action, and the small one is not a person liable for penalty for the action, so her mahr is not forfeited. Even if there is in the big one something that prevents considering her action, like insanity, etc., her right is not forfeited. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And he recovers it, i.e., the half mahr that he owes the small one. (Tahtawi) If she intentionally caused corruption: The restriction to intentional corruption regarding the husband's recourse against the big one for what he paid the small one; as for the forfeiture of the big one's mahr if it was before intercourse, intentional corruption is not required. Then intentional corruption occurs only if she breastfed without need and was aware of the existence of the marriage and knew that breastfeeding is corrupting. If any of these elements was missing, she is not intentional. For instance, if she thought the small one was hungry and breastfed her, then it turned out she was full, she is not intentional. The saying in that is her saying because no one else knows it. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And otherwise not: i.e., if she did not intentionally cause corruption, i.e., corruption of the marriage, by missing some element of breastfeeding without need, or knowledge of the existence of the marriage, or knowledge that breastfeeding is corruptive, he does not recover from the big one what he gave to the small one. Al-Shafi'i and Muhammad said: He recovers in both cases, whether she intentionally caused corruption or not, because she confirmed what was about to fall, which is half the mahr, and confirmation is like destruction. Our proof: She is a cause, not a direct agent, because she performed the breastfeeding, which is not a means to corrupt the marriage; rather it is a means to establish partial share (juz'iyyah). Corruption only occurs in this scenario by accident, and a cause is only liable by transgression and recourse. Zufar and Ahmad said this. According to Malik: He does not recover at all. The correct is what we said, because liability for causation is built on the attribute of transgression, which is intentional corruption. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:231) (Fath) No: i.e., he does not recover from her, and the saying in that is her saying with her oath if there is no evidence indicating her intentional corruption. (Tahtawi)
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed case within fosterage: if a man marries two women, one older (kabirah) and one younger (saghirah), and the older woman breastfeeds the younger one, both women become prohibited to the husband. The rationale is that he has now combined a mother and daughter through fosterage, which is forbidden. The Hadith quoted is: 'Marrying daughters prohibits mothers, and intercourse with mothers prohibits daughters.' The ruling varies based on whether the husband had consummated the marriage with the older wife before the breastfeeding. If not, he may remarry the younger wife after the separation, but the older wife is permanently prohibited as she becomes the mother of his (former) wife. If he had consummated, both are permanently prohibited. Regarding mahr: the older wife loses her mahr if separation occurred before consummation, because she caused the separation by her act. However, if she was coerced, asleep, insane, or the milk was administered without her direct action, she retains half the mahr. The younger wife always receives half the mahr because the separation was not from her side; she is not at fault. The husband can recover the half mahr he paid to the younger wife from the older wife if she intentionally caused the corruption. The definition of 'intentional' is strict: she must have breastfed without need, knowing the marriage existed, and knowing that breastfeeding would spoil it. If any condition is missing, she is not considered intentional and the husband cannot recover. There is a dispute: al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad hold that the husband can recover regardless of intent, because the older wife confirmed something about to fall (the younger wife's mahr). The Hanafi position is that only intentional wrongdoing makes the cause liable, as liability for causation requires transgression. This is supported by Zufar and Ahmad. Malik holds that there is no recourse at all. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the husband only recovers if the older wife intentionally caused the corruption, and her word is taken with oath unless there is evidence to the contrary.

Key Terms
ضرة (durrah): Co-wife (a wife sharing the same husband).
فساد النكاح (fasad al-nikah): Corruption of the marriage; here, the invalidation of the marriage due to fosterage.
مهر (mahr): The mandatory bridal gift from husband to wife.
تعمد الفساد (ta'ammud al-fasad): Intentional commission of an act that corrupts the marriage, knowing it would cause harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a big wife breastfeeds the small wife without knowing that it would spoil the marriage, what is the ruling on the husband's recourse for the half mahr of the small wife?
A) He recovers from the big wife regardless of her knowledge.
B) He does not recover because she was not intentional.
C) He recovers only if she intended to spoil the marriage.
D) He recovers only if she was coerced.

Key Takeaway
In fosterage between co-wives, both become forbidden; the mahr of the big wife depends on her intent and whether consummation occurred, and the husband can recover from her only if she intentionally caused corruption.

Fosterage and Its Effect on Mahr: The Hanafi Position
Financial consequences of fosterage on mahr in inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the younger wife's dower when fosterage invalidates her marriage, distinguish it from Maliki and Shafi'i positions, and apply the condition of intentional corruption to determine the husband's recourse.

Core Idea
The younger wife's dower is not forfeited – she is not liable for the nursing that broke the marriage.

Imagine a man marries a widow with a young daughter. Later, his first wife nurses that infant daughter, creating a foster relationship that invalidates the new marriage. What happens to the dower (mahr) he owes the younger wife? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the Hanafi answer: the younger wife keeps half her dower because the separation was not her fault. The husband can only reclaim that half from the older wife if she intentionally caused the corruption. We'll unpack this ruling and the key differences with other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the younger wife gets half the dower; the husband reclaims from the older wife only if she intentionally caused the corruption.
This is the mufta bihi from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Malik says the younger gets nothing because the separation came from her side. Shafi'i and Muhammad al-Shaybani say the husband reclaims in all cases, intentional or not.
Imam Muhammad is an intra-Hanafi difference here.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik: the nursing act is her action, so forfeiture applies. Shafi'i/Muhammad: the older wife confirmed what was about to fall (half mahr), which is like destruction.
Understand the logic behind each objection.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The younger is not liable because she is not 'ahl al-mujazat' (subject to recompense). For the older, she is only a cause (mutasabbib) and causation only binds with transgression (intentional corruption).
The key concept: transgression (ta'addi) is required for liability as a cause.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi, the younger keeps half; under Maliki, she gets nothing; under Shafi'i, the husband can always reclaim from the older. This affects financial outcomes significantly.
This difference matters in real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أحكام الرضاع
وللصغيرة نصفه ويرجع به على الكبيرة إن تعمدت الفساد وإلا لا، ويثبت بما يثبت به المال.
أي الزوج
أي قصد الكبيرة به أي وإن لم تتعمد الفساد
الرضاع
وللصغيرة نصفه : [ أي نصف المهر؛ لأن الفرقة قبل الدخول لا من قبلها. (ع)] وهذا عندنا، وقال مالك: لا يجب لها شيء؛ لأن الفرقة جاءت من قبلها؛ فإن الارتضاع فعلها، والفرقة باعتباره فسقط مهرها، ولنا: أن الفرقة لا من قبلها وفعلها غير معتبر في إسقاط حقها؛ لأن المهر إنما يسقط جزاء على الفعل، والصغيرة ليست من أهل المجازاة على الفعل، فلا يسقط مهرها حتى لو وجد في الكبيرة أيضاً ما يمنع اعتبار فعلها كالجنون وغيره لا يسقط حقها. (مستخلص فتح ويرجع به أي بنصف المهر الذي لزمه للصغيرة. (ط) إن تعمدت الفساد: التقييد بتعمد الفساد بالنسبة لرجوع الزوج على الكبيرة بما دفعه للصغيرة، أما سقوط مهر الكبيرة إن كان قبل الوطء فلا يشترط له تعمد الفساد، ثم تعمد الفساد إنما يكون إذا أرضعتها بلا حاجة وعلمت بقيام النكاح، وعلمت أن الإرضاع مفسد، فإن فاتت شيء منه لم تكن متعمدة، فلو ظنت أن الصغيرة جائعةً فأرضعتها ثم تبين أنها شبعانة لا تكون متعمدة، والقول في ذلك قولها؛ لأنه لا يقف عليه غيرها. (مستخلص، فتح) وإلا لا: أي وإن لم تتعمد الفساد أي فساد النكاح بأن فات شيء من الإرضاع بلا حاجة أو العلم بقيام النكاح أو العلم بالإرضاع المفسد لا يرجع بما أدى للصغيرة على الكبيرة، وقال الشافعي ومحمد: يرجع في الوجهين تعمدت الفساد أو لا؛ لأنها أكدت ما كان على شرف السقوط وهو نصف المهر، والتأكيد جار محرى الإتلاف، ولنا: أنها متسببة لا مباشرة؛ لأنها باشرت الإرضاع وهو ليس بموضوع؛ لإفساد النكاح بل هو سبب موضوع للجزئية، وإنما يثبت الفساد في هذه الصورة باتفاق الحال، والمتسبب إنما يضمن بالتعدي وبالرجوع وبه قال زفر وأحمد، وعند مالك: لا يرجع مطلقاً والأصح ما قلنا؛ لأن ضمان التسبب يبني على صفة التعدي وهو تعمد الفساد. رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۱/۱] (فتح)
لا: أي لا يرجع به عليها، والقول في ذلك قولها بيمينها إن لم توجد قرينة تدل على تعمدها الفساد. (ط) بما يثبت به المال: [وهو شهادة رجلين عدلين عاقلين بالغين حرين أو رجل وامرأتين كذلك. (ط)] لكن لا تقع الفرقة إلا بتفريق القاضي؛ لتضمنها إبطال حق العبد، ولا تقبل شهادة النساء المنفردات؛ لأن ثبوت الحرمة من لوازم الملك في باب النكاح، والملك لا يزول بشهادة النساء وحدهن فلا تثبت به الحرمة، وعند الشافعي: تثبت بشهادة أربع نسوة، وعند مالك بشهادة امرأة واحدة إن كانت موصوفة بالعدالة وعند أحمد: بمرضعة فقط، ولا فرق بين أن يكون الشهادة قبل النكاح أو بعده [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۱/۱] (فتح)
Book of Fosterage. Rulings of Fosterage. And for the younger (wife) is half of it, and he reclaims it from the older if she intentionally caused the corruption, otherwise not. And it is established by what establishes wealth. i.e., the husband. i.e., the older intended it. i.e., even if she did not intend the corruption. Fosterage: And for the younger is half of it: i.e., half the dower; because the separation occurred before consummation and not from her side. This is our view. Malik said: Nothing is obligatory for her because the separation came from her side; for nursing is her action, and the separation is attributed to it, so her dower is forfeited. Our proof: the separation is not from her side, and her action is not considered in forfeiting her right; because the dower is only forfeited as a recompense for the action, and the younger is not among those subject to recompense for actions, so her dower is not forfeited. Even if there existed in the older what prevents considering her action, like insanity etc., her right is not forfeited. (Mukhtasar Fath) And he reclaims it: i.e., half the dower that was due to the younger. (T) If she intentionally caused the corruption: the restriction to intentional corruption concerns the husband's recourse against the older for what he paid to the younger. As for the forfeiture of the older's dower if before intercourse, intentional corruption is not required. Then intentional corruption occurs only if she nursed her without need and knew the marriage existed and knew that nursing invalidates. If any of these is missing, she is not intentional. If she thought the younger was hungry and nursed her, then it turned out she was full, she is not intentional. The statement in that matter is hers because no one else can know it. (Mukhtasar, Fath) Otherwise not: i.e., if she did not intentionally cause corruption, i.e., corruption of the marriage, by missing some element of nursing without need, or knowledge of the marriage's existence, or knowledge that nursing is invalidating, he does not reclaim what he paid for the younger from the older. Al-Shafi'i and Muhammad said: he reclaims in both cases, whether she intentionally caused corruption or not, because she confirmed what was on the verge of falling, i.e., half the dower, and confirmation is akin to destruction. Our proof: she is a cause (mutasabbib) not a direct agent (mubashir); she directly performed nursing, but nursing is not legislated to invalidate marriage; rather it is a cause legislated for partiality (juz'iyyah). Invalidity is only established in this case by agreement of circumstances. The causer is only liable with transgression and recourse. Zufar and Ahmad said this. According to Malik, he does not reclaim at all. The correct is what we said because liability for causation is based on the attribute of transgression, which is intentional corruption. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/231 (Fath) No: i.e., he does not reclaim it from her. The statement in that matter is hers with her oath if no evidence indicates her intentional corruption. (T) By what establishes wealth: i.e., testimony of two just, sane, adult, free men, or one man and two women similarly. But separation only occurs by the judge's ruling because it involves nullifying a person's right. The testimony of women alone is not accepted because establishing prohibition is a consequence of ownership in marriage, and ownership is not removed by women's testimony alone, so prohibition is not established. According to al-Shafi'i, it is established by testimony of four women. According to Malik, by testimony of one woman if she is described as just. According to Ahmad, by a wet nurse alone. There is no difference whether the testimony is before or after marriage. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/231] (Fath)

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings when a wife (the elder) nurses her husband's infant daughter from another marriage, thereby establishing a foster relationship that invalidates the marriage. The text begins with the core ruling: the younger wife (the infant's mother) is entitled to half the dower (since separation occurred before consummation and not from her fault). The husband can reclaim that half from the older wife if she intentionally caused the corruption (i.e., she knowingly nursed with the intent to break the marriage). The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Malik holds that the younger wife gets nothing because the separation came from her side (the nursing is her action). The Hanafi response is that the younger wife is not legally responsible (not 'ahl al-mujazat') and her action is not considered for forfeiting her right. The text further explains the condition of 'intentional corruption': it requires that the older wife nursed without need (i.e., not out of necessity), knew the marriage existed, and knew that nursing invalidates marriage. If any element is missing, she is not considered intentional, and the husband cannot reclaim from her. The text then presents the views of al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) who hold that the husband can reclaim in all cases because the older wife confirmed what was about to fall. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the older wife is a cause (mutasabbib) not a direct agent, and causation only incurs liability with transgression. The passage ends with a discussion on evidence: fosterage is established by the same evidence as property claims (two men or a man and two women), and the separation only occurs by judge's ruling. The testimony of women alone is not accepted in this matter because it involves ownership (milk) in marriage.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage: breastfeeding that establishes a foster relationship preventing marriage.
المهر (al-mahr): Dower: obligatory payment from husband to wife upon marriage.
الفساد (al-fasad): Corruption: here meaning the invalidation of marriage due to foster relationship.
المتسبب (al-mutasabbib): Causer: one who indirectly causes a result, as opposed to a direct agent (mubashir).
التعدي (al-ta'addi): Transgression: exceeding legal limits, here specifically intentional corruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can the husband reclaim the half-mahr from the older wife who nursed his younger wife?
A) Whenever the fosterage invalidates the marriage.
B) Only if she intentionally caused the corruption by knowing the marriage and the effect.
C) Only if she was paid to nurse.
D) Only if the younger wife demands it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the younger wife retains half her dower when fosterage invalidates her marriage, and the husband can only reclaim it from the older wife if she intentionally caused the corruption.

What Constitutes Ila': Valid Oaths and the Shafi'i Dispute
Defines valid Ila' oaths and disputes with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which oaths constitute valid Ila' according to the Hanafi school, distinguish the intra-Hanafi disagreements, and explain the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
Any oath that prevents intercourse, even by conditional consequences, makes a husband a Mul.

Ila' is a husband's vow to abstain from his wife, with a four-month Qur'anic deadline. But what forms does this vow take? The Hanafi school expansively includes oaths by acts like Hajj, fasting, or charity, while al-Shafi'i restricts it to oaths by Allah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proofs, and the disputes within and outside the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basic Hanafi Rule
Any oath that prevents intercourse establishes Ila'. This includes direct oaths (e.g., 'I will not approach you for four months') and conditional oaths (e.g., 'If I approach you, I must do X').
The consequence must be serious enough to deter intercourse.
2
Distinguish Direct vs Conditional Oaths
The passage gives examples: swearing by Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, or divorce—either directly or conditionally. Conditional oaths are valid if the consequence is not easily avoidable.
Specified acts like 'fast this month' may allow waiting, so not Ila' according to the two Shaykhs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
The Qur'anic verse 'For those who swear off from their wives' is general; any oath that deters intercourse is included. The text also cites the reasoning that the consequence (e.g., Hajj) becomes due, so it acts as an effective deterrent.
The Shafi'i response is that the verse refers only to oaths by Allah's name.
4
Note Exceptions: Revocably Divorced, Irrevocably Divorced, Foreign Woman
Ila' from a revocably divorced woman (during 'idda) is valid because she remains a wife. From an irrevocably divorced or foreign woman, it is invalid because the marriage bond is absent.
Even if he later marries her, the Ila' does not become valid retrospectively.
5
Examine Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Two disputes are mentioned: (a) freeing a specified slave: Abu Yusuf says not Ila' because he can sell it; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes. (b) prayer and specified fasting: the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say not Ila' because they are easy to perform; Muhammad says yes.
Abu Yusuf initially agreed with Muhammad on prayer but later retracted.
6
Compare with the Shafi'i Position
Al-Shafi'i holds that Ila' is only by swearing by Allah, not by conditional consequences. The practical difference is that many Hanafi Ila' cases would not be Ila' for Shafi'is.
The Hanafi response is that the verse is general and includes any deterrent oath.

Source Text

No. If he swears by Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, divorce, or makes Ila' from a revocably divorced woman, he is a Mul; but from an irrevocably divorced or foreign woman, no. We say: The ruling in the text is attributed to the text, not to the meaning, and the revocably divorced is from our women by text because of the remaining marriage between them. According to Muhammad, he is a Mul, because it is an act of worship, and it is the first statement of Abu Yusuf. And al-Shafi'i said in one of his two sayings: "Ila' is only by Allah Almighty", i.e., it is not by condition and consequence. "And from the foreign woman" the discussion on its outcome is invalid due to the lack of legal capacity, so it does not become valid afterwards. So he is not a Mul regarding divorce, but without the expiration; because the condition for divorce by oath is the existence of marriage ownership at the time of conditioning or at the time of the existence of the condition, and it did not exist, so it is not valid for divorce, and it is valid regarding the expiration. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the ruling of Ila' (vow of abstinence). The text begins by stating the basic rule: if a man swears by Hajj, fasting, charity, manumission, or divorce, or makes Ila' from a revocably divorced woman, he becomes a Mul (one who has taken an oath of abstention). However, if he makes Ila' from an irrevocably divorced woman or a foreign (non-marriageable) woman, he does not become a Mul. The commentary then explains each part in detail. For the second type of Ila' (swearing with a condition and consequence), it gives examples: if he says 'If I approach you, I must perform Hajj' etc., that is Ila' because the consequence prevents intercourse. Specified acts like fasting a specific month may not constitute Ila' if he can wait until the month ends and then approach without consequence. There is a dispute with Abu Yusuf regarding a specified slave: Abu Yusuf says he can sell the slave to avoid the consequence, so it is not Ila', while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the sale is uncertain and does not prevent Ila'. The passage also addresses a hypothetical objection: how can Ila' apply to a revocably divorced woman who has no right to intercourse? The answer is that the ruling is based on the text (Qur'an) which includes such women due to remaining matrimonial bond. Regarding the Shafi'i view, al-Shafi'i holds that Ila' is only by swearing by Allah, not by conditional consequences. Finally, for a woman who is irrevocably divorced or a foreign woman, Ila' is invalid because the marriage bond is not present, and even if he later marries her, it does not become valid. However, the oath may still be valid in terms of requiring expiation if broken, but not for triggering divorce by passage of time.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by the husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
مول (mūlī): The husband who has taken the oath of Ila'.
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqa raj‘iyya): A woman who has been divorced with a revocable divorce (first or second divorce where the husband can take her back during her 'idda).
مبانة (mubāna): A woman irrevocably divorced (third divorce or faskh), where the marriage is completely severed.
كفارة (kaffāra): Expiation for breaking an oath, usually fasting three days or feeding ten poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT constitute a valid Ila'?
A) A husband says: 'If I approach you, I will fast for one month.'
B) A husband says: 'I swear by Allah I will not touch you for four months.'
C) A husband says: 'If I approach you, I will pray two rak'ahs.'
D) A husband says to his revocably divorced wife: 'If I take you back, I will not approach you for four months.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines Ila' broadly: any oath, direct or conditional, that effectively prevents intercourse for four months or more, even if not by Allah's name, with the key exception that the wife must be a wife or revocably divorced at the time of the oath.

Duration of Ila' for a Slave Woman and Verbal Fay' When Unable
Duration for slave woman and causes for verbal fay'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Ila' period for a slave woman and explain the conditions under which verbal fay' is permitted.

Core Idea
A slave woman's Ila' period is two months, halved like 'idda; when intercourse is impossible, verbal fay' suffices.

This passage tackles two interconnected issues within the law of Ila' (vow of abstention from intercourse). First, it establishes that the duration for a slave wife is two months, not four, and provides the Hanafi rationale based on analogy with the 'idda period. Then it lists several impediments—illness, obstruction, distance—that make actual intercourse impossible, and rules that in such cases the husband may fulfill his return (fay') verbally. Understanding this shows how the Hanafi school uses analogy (qiyas) and the concept of substitutes (khalaf) to preserve the purpose of the law while accommodating necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on duration
Locate the explicit statement: the Ila' period for a slave woman is two months. Note that this includes both cases where the husband is free or slave.
The passage says 'ومدة إيلاء الأمة شهران'.
2
Understand the Hanafi reasoning and the Shafi'i objection
Read the commentary: Hanafis analogize the period to 'idda, which is halved for slaves, because both are terms set for separation. Shafi'is view the period as a means to manifest oppression from withholding the right to intercourse, which is equal for free and slave women, so no halving.
This is a classic ikhtilaf based on different perceptions of the 'illa (effective cause).
3
List the causes of inability that allow verbal fay'
Identify the five impediments mentioned: husband's illness, wife's illness, ratq (obstruction), wife's young age, and distance. In these cases, the husband cannot cohabit, so his fay' is accomplished by saying 'I have returned' or similar.
Verbal fay' is a substitute (khalaf) for intercourse, valid only when intercourse is impossible.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., slave wife, husband paralyzed), determine the Ila' period and the valid method of fay'. State that the period is two months, and since intercourse is impossible, verbal fay' is sufficient.
If the slave wife is freed during the Ila' period, the remaining period changes to four months.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The duration of Ila' of a slave woman is two months. If the husband is unable to have intercourse with her due to his illness, her illness, or due to rutaq (obstruction), i.e., the married woman, or due to her young age, or due to distance, then his fay' (return) is that he says, i.e., due to her young age, i.e., due to his illness, i.e., due to her illness. 'The duration of Ila' etc.' meaning: the married slave woman, its absolute (use) includes even if her husband is free. If she is freed during it, she transfers to the duration of free women. And this is apparent that Ila' is not invalidated by her emancipation, rather it remains. And al-Shafi'i said – may Allah have mercy on him – the duration of Ila' of a slave woman is four months. This is based on the fact that according to him this duration was set to show the oppression by preventing the right to intercourse, and the free woman and the slave woman are equal in that. According to us, the duration was set as a term for separation, so it resembles the duration of 'idda, so it becomes half due to slavery because it is from the rights of marriage. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3:179] 'Have intercourse with her': i.e., about intercourse with his wife from whom he made Ila'. (c) 'Due to rutaq': i.e., due to rutaq, which is obstruction of the mouth of the uterus with flesh, bone, or similar. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:274] 'Then his fay' is that he says etc.': i.e., the husband's return in these situations. (t)
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage discusses two aspects of Ila': the duration for a slave wife and the circumstances that allow the husband to make fay' (return) verbally instead of through intercourse. The text first states that the Ila' period for a slave woman is two months, not four months as for a free woman. The commentary explains that the term 'slave woman' here includes both cases where the husband is free or slave; if the slave wife is freed during the Ila' period, the period changes to that of a free woman (four months). The justification given is that according to the Hanafi school, the period of Ila' is set as a term for separation (ajal for baynuna), resembling the 'idda period, and thus it is halved due to slavery. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, because he sees the period as serving to manifest the oppression of preventing the right to intercourse, which is equal for free and slave women. Then the passage lists instances where the husband is unable to have intercourse: due to his illness, her illness, an obstruction (ratq) in her vagina, her young age, or long distance. In these cases, the husband may make fay' verbally by saying 'I have returned' or similar. This is a substitute (khalaf) for actual intercourse.

Key Terms
رتق (ratq): An obstruction in the vagina that prevents intercourse, often due to flesh or bone.
فيء (fay’): Return to the wife by ending the vow of abstention; can be through intercourse or verbally when unable.
أمة منكوحة (ama mankūḥa): A slave woman who is legally married (though ownership by husband is separate).

Key Terms from Source Passage
